<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Civilization</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="contentSub2"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Complex society</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Civilization_(disambiguation)" title="Civilization (disambiguation)">Civilization (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Egypt.Giza.Sphinx.02.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" decoding="async" height="248" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Egypt.Giza.Sphinx.02.jpg/330px-Egypt.Giza.Sphinx.02.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Egypt.Giza.Sphinx.02.jpg/495px-Egypt.Giza.Sphinx.02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Egypt.Giza.Sphinx.02.jpg/660px-Egypt.Giza.Sphinx.02.jpg 2x" width="330"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Egypt.Giza.Sphinx.02.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ancient Egypt provides a canonical example of an early culture considered a civilization.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-1">[1]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>A <b>civilization</b> (or <b>civilisation</b>) is any <a href="/wiki/Complex_society" title="Complex society">complex society</a> characterized by the development of <a href="/wiki/State_(polity)" title="State (polity)">the state</a>, <a href="/wiki/Social_stratification" title="Social stratification">social stratification</a>,  <a href="/wiki/Urban_area" title="Urban area">urbanization</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Symbol" title="Symbol">symbolic</a> systems of communication beyond <a href="/wiki/Natural_language" title="Natural language">natural spoken language</a> (namely, a <a href="/wiki/Writing_system" title="Writing system">writing system</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Adams_1966_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-Adams_1966-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Haviland_2013_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Haviland_2013-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wright_2004_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wright_2004-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Llobera_2003_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-Llobera_2003-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fernández-Armesto_2001_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fernández-Armesto_2001-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boyden_2004_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Boyden_2004-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Solms-Laubach_2007_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Solms-Laubach_2007-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-9">[9]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AthensAcropolisDawnAdj06028.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/AthensAcropolisDawnAdj06028.jpg/330px-AthensAcropolisDawnAdj06028.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/AthensAcropolisDawnAdj06028.jpg/495px-AthensAcropolisDawnAdj06028.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/AthensAcropolisDawnAdj06028.jpg/660px-AthensAcropolisDawnAdj06028.jpg 2x" width="330"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AthensAcropolisDawnAdj06028.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Acropolis_of_Athens" title="Acropolis of Athens">Acropolis of Athens</a>: <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a> is widely referred to by many as the <a href="/wiki/Cradle_of_civilization" title="Cradle of civilization">cradle</a> of <a class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Western_civilization" title="Western civilization">Western civilization</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Democracy#History" title="Democracy">birthplace of democracy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Civilizations are intimately associated with additional characteristics such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Centralization" title="Centralization">centralization</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Domestication" title="Domestication">domestication</a> of plant and animal species (including humans), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Division_of_labor" title="Division of labor">specialization of labour</a>, culturally-ingrained <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Idea_of_Progress" title="Idea of Progress">ideologies of progress</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monument" title="Monument">monumental</a> <a href="/wiki/Architecture" title="Architecture">architecture</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taxation" title="Taxation">taxation</a>, societal dependence upon <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Farming" title="Farming">farming</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Expansionism" title="Expansionism">expansionism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Haviland_2013_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-Haviland_2013-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wright_2004_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-Wright_2004-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Llobera_2003_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-Llobera_2003-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boyden_2004_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-Boyden_2004-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Solms-Laubach_2007_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-Solms-Laubach_2007-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-9">[9]</a></sup>
</p><p>Historically, a civilization has often been understood as a larger and "more advanced" <a href="/wiki/Culture" title="Culture">culture</a>, in implied contrast to smaller, supposedly less advanced cultures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Adams_1966_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-Adams_1966-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wright_2004_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-Wright_2004-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Llobera_2003_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-Llobera_2003-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-:4-12">[12]</a></sup> In this broad sense, a civilization contrasts with non-centralized tribal societies, including the cultures of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nomadic_pastoralist" title="Nomadic pastoralist">nomadic pastoralists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> societies or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hunter-gather" title="Hunter-gather">hunter-gatherers</a>; however, sometimes it also contrasts with the cultures found within civilizations themselves. Civilizations are organized densely-populated settlements divided into <a href="/wiki/Hierarchy" title="Hierarchy">hierarchical</a> <a href="/wiki/Social_class" title="Social class">social classes</a> with a ruling elite and subordinate urban and rural populations, which engage in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intensive_agriculture" title="Intensive agriculture">intensive agriculture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mining" title="Mining">mining</a>, small-scale manufacture and <a href="/wiki/Trade" title="Trade">trade</a>. Civilization concentrates power, extending human control over the rest of nature, including over other human beings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-:5-13">[13]</a></sup>
</p><p>Civilization, as its etymology (see <a href="#History_of_the_concept">below</a>) suggests, is a concept originally associated with <a href="/wiki/Town" title="Town">towns</a> and cities. The earliest emergence of civilizations is generally connected with the final stages of the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic_Revolution" title="Neolithic Revolution">Neolithic Revolution</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Asia" title="West Asia">West Asia</a>, culminating in the relatively rapid process of <a href="/wiki/Urban_revolution" title="Urban revolution">urban revolution</a> and <a href="/wiki/State_formation" title="State formation">state-formation</a>, a political development associated with the appearance of a governing elite.
</p>
