The <a href="/wiki/Maya_civilization" title="Maya civilization">Maya civilization</a> is noted for its <a href="/wiki/Maya_script" title="Maya script">logosyllabic script</a>—the most sophisticated and highly developed <a href="/wiki/Writing_system" title="Writing system">writing system</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pre-Columbian_era" title="Pre-Columbian era">pre-Columbian</a> <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>—as well as for its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maya_art" title="Maya art">art</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maya_architecture" title="Maya architecture">architecture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maya_numerals" title="Maya numerals">mathematics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maya_calendar" title="Maya calendar">calendar</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Maya_astronomy" title="Maya astronomy">astronomical</a> system.

<p><a href="/wiki/Notre-Dame_de_Paris" title="Notre-Dame de Paris">Notre-Dame de Paris</a> in <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> is among the most recognizable symbols of the civilization of <a href="/wiki/Christendom" title="Christendom">Christendom</a>. <a class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Western_civilization" title="Western civilization">Western civilization</a> is most strongly influenced by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greco-Roman" title="Greco-Roman">Greco-Roman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Christian_culture" title="Christian culture">Christian</a> cultures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PerryChase2012_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-PerryChase2012-90">[90]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> has played a <a href="/wiki/Role_of_Christianity_in_civilization" title="Role of Christianity in civilization">prominent role</a> in the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Western_civilization" title="History of Western civilization">shaping of Western civilization</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Caltron_J.H_Hayas_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-Caltron_J.H_Hayas-95">[95]</a></sup>

<div class="thumb" style="width: 232px;"><div style="margin:-0.16666666666667px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hagia_Sophia_Mars_2013.jpg" title="Hagia Sophia in Istanbul, Turkey. An architectural and cultural icon of Byzantine and Eastern Orthodox civilization.[96][97][98] Its influence, both architecturally and liturgically, was widespread and enduring in the Eastern Christianity, Western Christianity, and Ottoman architecture.[98] Represents the legacy of the Byzantine Empire one of the most powerful economic, cultural, and military force in Europe,[99] noted for its art, architecture, science, medicine, and law.[100]"><img alt="Hagia Sophia in Istanbul, Turkey. An architectural and cultural icon of Byzantine and Eastern Orthodox civilization.[96][97][98] Its influence, both architecturally and liturgically, was widespread and enduring in the Eastern Christianity, Western Christianity, and Ottoman architecture.[98] Represents the legacy of the Byzantine Empire one of the most powerful economic, cultural, and military force in Europe,[99] noted for its art, architecture, science, medicine, and law.[100]" data-file-height="3681" data-file-width="5514" decoding="async" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Hagia_Sophia_Mars_2013.jpg/348px-Hagia_Sophia_Mars_2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Hagia_Sophia_Mars_2013.jpg/523px-Hagia_Sophia_Mars_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Hagia_Sophia_Mars_2013.jpg/697px-Hagia_Sophia_Mars_2013.jpg 2x" width="232"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/Hagia_Sophia" title="Hagia Sophia">Hagia Sophia</a> in <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>. An architectural and <a href="/wiki/Cultural_icon" title="Cultural icon">cultural icon</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Byzantine_culture" title="Byzantine culture">Byzantine</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Culture" title="Eastern Orthodox Culture">Eastern Orthodox civilization</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M130_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-M130-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Heinle_&amp;_Schlaich_1996_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-Heinle_&amp;_Schlaich_1996-98">[98]</a></sup> Its influence, both architecturally and liturgically, was widespread and enduring in the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Christianity" title="Eastern Christianity">Eastern Christianity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Western_Christianity" title="Western Christianity">Western Christianity</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_architecture" title="Ottoman architecture">Ottoman architecture</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Heinle_&amp;_Schlaich_1996_98-1"><a href="#cite_note-Heinle_&amp;_Schlaich_1996-98">[98]</a></sup> Represents the legacy of the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a> one of the most powerful economic, cultural, and military force in Europe,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M19_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-M19-99">[99]</a></sup> noted for its <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_art" title="Byzantine art">art</a>, <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_architecture" title="Byzantine architecture">architecture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_science" title="Byzantine science">science</a>, <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_medicine" title="Byzantine medicine">medicine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_law" title="Byzantine law">law</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup>
</p>

<p>The <a href="/wiki/Round_city_of_Baghdad" title="Round city of Baghdad">Round city of Baghdad</a> was founded by caliph <a href="/wiki/Al-Mansur" title="Al-Mansur">Al-Mansur</a> in 762–766 CE as the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Abbasid_Caliphate" title="Abbasid Caliphate">Abbasid Caliphate</a>, setting the stage for the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age" title="Islamic Golden Age">Islamic Golden Age</a> beginning with the subsequent construction of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Wisdom" title="House of Wisdom">House of Wisdom</a>. It is the fabled city in <a href="/wiki/One_Thousand_and_One_Nights" title="One Thousand and One Nights">One Thousand and One Nights</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Netton_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-Netton-101">[101]</a></sup>

<div class="thumb" style="width: 234px;"><div style="margin:-0.16666666666667px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Panoramic_views_of_Borobudur.jpg" title="Borobudur in Indonesia is the world's largest Buddhist monument and represents the Javanese empire of Mataram kingdom,[102][103][104] a prominent seaborne civilization and center of scholarship whose religious, cultural, political, and economic influence spread throughout Southeast Asia and into China, India, Tibet, and Korea.[104][105][106][107][108]"><img alt="Borobudur in Indonesia is the world's largest Buddhist monument and represents the Javanese and Malay empire of Srivijaya, a prominent seaborne civilization and center of scholarship whose religious, cultural, political, and economic influence spread throughout Southeast Asia and into China, India, Tibet, and Korea." data-file-height="1116" data-file-width="1689" decoding="async" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Panoramic_views_of_Borobudur.jpg/351px-Panoramic_views_of_Borobudur.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Panoramic_views_of_Borobudur.jpg/528px-Panoramic_views_of_Borobudur.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Panoramic_views_of_Borobudur.jpg/704px-Panoramic_views_of_Borobudur.jpg 2x" width="234"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/Borobudur" title="Borobudur">Borobudur</a> in <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> is the world's largest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhist" title="Buddhist">Buddhist</a> monument and represents the <a href="/wiki/Javanese_people" title="Javanese people">Javanese</a> empire of <a href="/wiki/Mataram_Kingdom" title="Mataram Kingdom">Mataram kingdom</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zakharov_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-Zakharov-103">[103]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dellios_and_Ferguson_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dellios_and_Ferguson-104">[104]</a></sup> a prominent <a href="/wiki/Thalassocracy" title="Thalassocracy">seaborne</a> civilization and center of scholarship whose religious, cultural, political, and economic influence spread throughout <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a> and into <a href="/wiki/History_of_China" title="History of China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_India" title="History of India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tibet" title="Tibet">Tibet</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Korea" title="Korea">Korea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dellios_and_Ferguson_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-Dellios_and_Ferguson-104">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sen_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-sen-107">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup>

<div class="thumb" style="width: 232px;"><div style="margin:-0.16666666666667px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:St._Basil_Cathedral.jpg" title="Saint Basil's Cathedral in Moscow; the most popular icon of Russian civilization.[109] Russian civilization has had a considerable influence on global culture, it also has a rich material culture and a tradition in science and technology."><img alt="Saint Basil's Cathedral in Moscow; the most popular icon of Russian civilization.[109] Russian civilization has had a considerable influence on global culture, it also has a rich material culture and a tradition in science and technology." data-file-height="2362" data-file-width="3543" decoding="async" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/St._Basil_Cathedral.jpg/348px-St._Basil_Cathedral.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/St._Basil_Cathedral.jpg/524px-St._Basil_Cathedral.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/St._Basil_Cathedral.jpg/698px-St._Basil_Cathedral.jpg 2x" width="232"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/Saint_Basil%27s_Cathedral" title="Saint Basil's Cathedral">Saint Basil's Cathedral</a> in Moscow; the most popular icon of <a href="/wiki/Russian_civilization" title="Russian civilization">Russian civilization</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Russian_civilization" title="Russian civilization">Russian civilization</a> has had a considerable influence on <a href="/wiki/Cross-cultural_studies" title="Cross-cultural studies">global culture</a>, it also has a rich <a href="/wiki/Material_culture" title="Material culture">material culture</a> and a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Russian_inventions_and_technology_records" title="Timeline of Russian inventions and technology records">tradition in science and technology</a>.
</p>
</div>
</div></li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 277.33333333333px"><div style="width: 277.33333333333px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 275.33333333333px;"><div style="margin:-0.16666666666667px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ankor_Wat_temple.jpg" title="Angkor Wat in Cambodia is the largest religious structure ever constructed in human history[110] and represents the legacy of the Khmer Empire, one of the most influential civilizations of Southeast Asia and home to the world's biggest preindustrial city by area.[111][112]"><img alt="Angkor Wat in Cambodia is the largest religious structure ever constructed in human history[110] and represents the legacy of the Khmer Empire, one of the most influential civilizations of Southeast Asia and home to the world's biggest preindustrial city by area.[111][112]" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="1280" decoding="async" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Ankor_Wat_temple.jpg/413px-Ankor_Wat_temple.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Ankor_Wat_temple.jpg/621px-Ankor_Wat_temple.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Ankor_Wat_temple.jpg/827px-Ankor_Wat_temple.jpg 2x" width="276"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/Angkor_Wat" title="Angkor Wat">Angkor Wat</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">Cambodia</a> is the largest religious structure ever constructed in <a href="/wiki/Human_history" title="Human history">human history</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> and represents the legacy of the <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Empire" title="Khmer Empire">Khmer Empire</a>, one of the most influential civilizations of <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a> and home to the world's <a href="/wiki/Angkor" title="Angkor">biggest preindustrial city</a> by area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bang_et_al._111-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bang_et_al.-111">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Evans_et_al._112-0"><a href="#cite_note-Evans_et_al.-112">[112]</a></sup>
</p>
</div>
</div></li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 228.66666666667px"><div style="width: 228.66666666667px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 226.66666666667px;"><div style="margin:-0.16666666666667px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nineveh_-_Mashki_Gate.jpg" title="Nineveh was an ancient Assyrian city of Upper Mesopotamia, the Assyrian civilization noted for its sculpture, architecture, literature, law and astronomy. Modern Assyrians are Syriac Christians who claim descent from Assyria, one of the oldest civilizations in the world, dating back to 2500 BC in ancient Mesopotamia.[113]"><img alt="Nineveh was an ancient Assyrian city of Upper Mesopotamia, the Assyrian civilization noted for its sculpture, architecture, literature, law and astronomy. Modern Assyrians are Syriac Christians who claim descent from Assyria, one of the oldest civilizations in the world, dating back to 2500 BC in ancient Mesopotamia.[113]" data-file-height="3696" data-file-width="5405" decoding="async" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Nineveh_-_Mashki_Gate.jpg/340px-Nineveh_-_Mashki_Gate.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Nineveh_-_Mashki_Gate.jpg/511px-Nineveh_-_Mashki_Gate.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Nineveh_-_Mashki_Gate.jpg/680px-Nineveh_-_Mashki_Gate.jpg 2x" width="227"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/Nineveh" title="Nineveh">Nineveh</a> was an ancient <a href="/wiki/Assyria" title="Assyria">Assyrian</a> city of <a href="/wiki/Upper_Mesopotamia" title="Upper Mesopotamia">Upper Mesopotamia</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Assyrian_civilization" title="Assyrian civilization">Assyrian civilization</a> noted for its <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_sculpture" title="Assyrian sculpture">sculpture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Mesopotamia" title="Architecture of Mesopotamia">architecture</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Assyrian_literature" title="Assyrian literature">literature</a>, <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_law" title="Assyrian law">law</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Assyrian_astronomy" title="Assyrian astronomy">astronomy</a>. Modern <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_people" title="Assyrian people">Assyrians</a> are <a href="/wiki/Syriac_Christianity" title="Syriac Christianity">Syriac Christians</a> who <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_continuity" title="Assyrian continuity">claim descent from Assyria</a>, one of the oldest civilizations in the world, dating back to 2500 BC in ancient <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup>
</p>
</div>
</div></li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 180.66666666667px"><div style="width: 180.66666666667px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 178.66666666667px;"><div style="margin:-0.16666666666667px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lalibela,_san_giorgio,_esterno_24.jpg" title="Lalibela churches; among the most popular icon of Ethiopia, and represents the legacy of the Kingdom of Aksum, a Classical African civilization.[114]"><img alt="Lalibela churches; among the most popular icon of Ethiopia, and represents the legacy of the Kingdom of Aksum, a Classical African civilization.[114]" data-file-height="5848" data-file-width="6748" decoding="async" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Lalibela%2C_san_giorgio%2C_esterno_24.jpg/268px-Lalibela%2C_san_giorgio%2C_esterno_24.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Lalibela%2C_san_giorgio%2C_esterno_24.jpg/403px-Lalibela%2C_san_giorgio%2C_esterno_24.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Lalibela%2C_san_giorgio%2C_esterno_24.jpg/537px-Lalibela%2C_san_giorgio%2C_esterno_24.jpg 2x" width="179"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/Lalibela" title="Lalibela">Lalibela</a> churches; among the most popular icon of <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>, and represents the legacy of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Aksum" title="Kingdom of Aksum">Kingdom of Aksum</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Classical_African_civilization" title="Classical African civilization">Classical African civilization</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-libraries_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-libraries-114">[114]</a></sup>
</p>
</div>
</div></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-human_civilizations">Non-human civilizations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Civilization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Non-human civilizations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The current scientific consensus is that human beings are the only animal species with the cognitive ability to create civilizations that has emerged on Earth. A recent thought experiment, the <a href="/wiki/Silurian_hypothesis" title="Silurian hypothesis">silurian hypothesis</a>, however, considers whether it would "be possible to detect an industrial civilization in the geological record" given the paucity of geological information about eras before the <a href="/wiki/Quaternary" title="Quaternary">quaternary</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup>
</p><p>Astronomers speculate about the existence of communicating intelligent civilizations within and beyond the Milky Way galaxy, usually using variants of the <a href="/wiki/Drake_equation" title="Drake equation">Drake equation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-APJ-20200615_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-APJ-20200615-116">[116]</a></sup> They also conduct <a href="/wiki/Search_for_extraterrestrial_intelligence" title="Search for extraterrestrial intelligence">searches for such intelligences</a> – such as for technological traces, called "<a href="/wiki/Technosignature" title="Technosignature">technosignatures</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10.1016/j.actaastro.2021.02.029_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-10.1016/j.actaastro.2021.02.029-117">[117]</a></sup> The proposed proto-scientific field "<a href="/wiki/Xenoarchaeology" title="Xenoarchaeology">xenoarchaeology</a>" is concerned with the study of artifact remains of non-human civilizations to reconstruct and interpret past lives of alien societies if such get discovered and confirmed scientifically.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-:7-15"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-:7_15-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">It remains the most influential sociological study of the topic, spawning its own body of secondary literature. Notably, <a href="/wiki/Hans_Peter_Duerr" title="Hans Peter Duerr">Hans Peter Duerr</a> attacked it in a major work (3,500 pages in five volumes, published 1988–2002). Elias, at the time a nonagenarian, was still able to respond to the criticism the year before his death. In 2002, Duerr was himself criticized by Michael Hinz's <i>Der Zivilisationsprozeß: Mythos oder Realität</i> (2002), saying that his criticism amounted to hateful defamation of Elias, through excessive standards of <a href="/wiki/Political_correctness" title="Political correctness">political correctness</a>.  <i><a href="/wiki/Der_Spiegel" title="Der Spiegel">Der Spiegel</a></i> <a class="external text" href="http://www.spiegel.de/spiegel/print/d-25327104.html" rel="nofollow">40/2002</a> <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20190228225831/http://www.spiegel.de/spiegel/print/d-25327104.html" rel="nofollow">Archived</a> 28 February 2019 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-:8-16"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-:8_16-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Albert Schweitzer. The Philosophy of Civilization, trans. C.T. Campion (Amherst, NY: Prometheus Books, 1987), p. 91.</span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-:9-19"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-:9_19-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">E.g. in the title <i>A narrative of the loss of the Winterton East Indiaman wrecked on the coast of Madagascar in 1792; and of the sufferings connected with that event. <li id="cite_note-:10-20"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-:10_20-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"Civilization" (1974), <i><a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica" title="Encyclopædia Britannica">Encyclopædia Britannica</a></i> 15th ed. Vol. II, Encyclopædia Britannica, Inc., 956. Retrieved 25 August 2007. Using the terms "civilization" and "culture" as equivalents are controversial<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (October 2014)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and generally rejected so that for example some types of culture are not normally described as civilizations.</span>
</li>
